# Running a Profitable Business: Understanding Financial Ratios

> Financial ratios—such as ROI (return on investment) or ROA (return on assets)— are a valuable tool for measuring a company's progress against a financial goal, a certain competitor, or the overall industry. In this course, professors Jim and Kay Stice explain the financial ratios found on balance sheets, income statements, and cash-flow statements and provide examples from real-world companies suc

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios) | 1h 49m | Beginner | 322K learners
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

## Table of Contents

### Chapter Overview

- [**Introduction**](#introduction) (1 videos)
  - Gain financial insights
- [**1. What Is Financial Ratio Analysis?**](#1-what-is-financial-ratio-analysis) (1 videos)
  - Introduction to financial ratio analysis
- [**2. A Review of the Financial Statements**](#2-a-review-of-the-financial-statements) (4 videos)
  - What are the financial statements?
  - The balance sheet
  - The income statement
  - The statement of cash flows
- [**3. The DuPont Framework**](#3-the-dupont-framework) (5 videos)
  - The DuPont company: creating accounting history
  - Return on equity
  - DuPont framework
  - DuPont framework: Target and Walmart
  - Problem description to explanation
- [**4. Common-Size Financial Statements**](#4-common-size-financial-statements) (4 videos)
  - Olympic medals and GDP per capita
  - Common size overview
  - Target's common-size income statement
  - Target's common-size balance sheet
- [**5. Profitability Ratios**](#5-profitability-ratios) (4 videos)
  - McDonald's most profitable items
  - Comparing profitability with financial ratios
  - Specific profitability ratios
  - Price-earnings ratio
- [**6. Efficiency Ratios**](#6-efficiency-ratios) (5 videos)
  - Mark-up vs. profitability: Harry Winston vs. Walmart
  - Number of days' sales in inventory
  - Average collection period
  - Length of the operating cycle
  - Fixed asset turnover and other utilization ratios
- [**7. Leverage Ratios**](#7-leverage-ratios) (3 videos)
  - Singapore Airlines' low leverage
  - Current ratio
  - Leverage ratios
- [**8. Potential Pitfalls to Ratio Analysis**](#8-potential-pitfalls-to-ratio-analysis) (3 videos)
  - Historical data pitfalls and baseball
  - Excess data and comparability issues
  - "Smoking gun" and historical data biases
- [**Conclusion**](#conclusion) (1 videos)
  - What financial ratio analysis can NOT do

>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=5)** - I'm also a professor of accounting at Brigham Young University.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=8)** We are an accounting family.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=10)** - Absolutely.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=11)** We love numbers.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=12)** We love financial statements, and we love using financial reports to gain insights into how companies work.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=18)** - [Kay] This course introduces you to methods of financial ratio analysis that'll allow you to use a company's financial reports to identify the company's strengths and weaknesses.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=28)** - [Jim] You can use a company's financial reports to identify areas for improvement, as well as to identify areas of risk.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=34)** - [Kay] Before taking this course, you might consider taking our accounting fundamentals course.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=39)** That course introduces you to the major areas of accounting.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=43)** - But with that said, we have designed this financial ratio analysis course to be self-contained.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=48)** And we carefully explain any accounting terminology that we use.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=52)** - In short, this is an introductory course with no prior accounting knowledge necessary.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=57)** - So what can you learn using financial ratio analysis?
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=61)** Well, you can learn how much Walmart marks up its items that it sells to you.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=64)** - In other words, when Walmart sells you an item for $10, how much did Walmart have to pay to buy that item?
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=71)** - You can also learn how many days, on average, items hang on the racks and sit on the shelves at Nordstrom before they're sold.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=78)** The answer is about 60 days.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=79)** - You can learn the same thing about the food at McDonald's.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=82)** Hopefully the answer is substantially less than 60 days.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=85)** - Financial ratio analysis is the process of using the relationships among a company's financial numbers to gain insights into that company's operations.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/gain-financial-insights?u=76281980&t=94)** - Let's go!

### 1. What Is Financial Ratio Analysis?

> [↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### Introduction to financial ratio analysis
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - Now, when it comes to financial ratio analysis, I like to borrow a quote from Winston Churchill.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=5)** He said the following.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=7)** "The further backward you can look, "the further forward you can see."
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=10)** We analyze financial ratios to tell us if a company has done well or poorly in the past and to help us see how the company might do in the future.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=18)** That brings us to financial ratio analysis, which is simply the examination of relationships among financial statement numbers.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=25)** We're going to do a lot of dividing one number by another to draw conclusions.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=30)** When it comes to ratio analysis, we're going to do two types.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=34)** One, we're going to compare the same company across time to see how the company has performed over time.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=41)** And secondly, at the same point in time, we're going to compare across companies.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=46)** We'll begin our discussion by looking at a company most of us are familiar with, Target, a retailer.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=52)** In 2013, they reported income of $2 billion.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=55)** Is that a lot?
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=57)** At the end of 2013, they reported total assets of $45 billion.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=61)** Is that a lot?
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=63)** What'd they do with those assets?
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=65)** The end of 2013, they had liabilities of $28 billion.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=69)** Is that a lot?
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=70)** And what'd they use that money for?
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=72)** When it comes to financial ratio analysis, we'll do both diagnostic and prognostic analysis.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=78)** Diagnostic analysis tells us where might a company have problems now?
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=84)** Prognostic tells how might they do in the future?
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=88)** Let's consider, to illustrate that, the example of GAAP.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=91)** Now, common methods of analysis, we'll do common size financial statements.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=97)** We prepare common size financial statements by dividing financial statement numbers by either total sales or total assets.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=104)** And we'll also do ratio analysis, which involves relationships between financial statement numbers.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=110)** We'll use one of my favorite things in all of accounting, the DuPont framework, which tells us about the profitability, the efficiency, and the leverage of a company, how that company is doing on those three dimensions.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=122)** When it comes to financial ratio analysis, there's a four-step process.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=126)** First, we'll use the DuPont framework to break down return on equity into its component parts.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=131)** Return on equity is a general overall measure of how well a firm is doing.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=136)** Once we've done the DuPont framework, we'll prepare common size financial statements.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=141)** Step three will involve using additional ratios to assess a firm's profitability, efficiency, and leverage.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=148)** Based on these first three steps, we should be able to identify individuals that we need to speak to about the financial results.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=156)** Again, ratio analysis will lead us to people and help us answer the right questions to determine how can we make the future different?
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/introduction-to-financial-ratio-analysis-2?u=76281980&t=165)** We'll see these four steps throughout this course as we do for our financial ratio analysis.

### 2. A Review of the Financial Statements

> [↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### What are the financial statements?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - What's a balance sheet?
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=1)** - Well, a balance sheet is a listing of a company's valuable resources, its assets, and a listing of where the company got the money to buy those assets.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=9)** - Where do companies get money to buy assets?
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=12)** - Well, there are three general sources.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=14)** First, they can borrow it.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=16)** Second, the owners can take money from their private savings and invest it in the business.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=21)** And third, the company can generate profits that are then kept in the business to buy more assets.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=26)** - [Interviewer] Okay, a balance sheet is a listing of a company's assets and the sources of financing to buy those assets.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=31)** - [Expert] Correct.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=32)** - So, what's an income statement?
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=34)** - That's easy.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=35)** An income statement is a report telling how much money a company made during the month or the quarter or the year, whatever period is covered by the income statement.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=43)** - It seems like people are always talking about companies' income statements.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=46)** - You often hear in the business news about a company's net income.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=50)** - I've also heard about a statement of cash flows.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=53)** What's that?
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=53)** - Well, let me give you a little lesson in accounting terminology.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=56)** When in doubt, say it slowly.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=59)** So, what is a statement of cash flows?
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=61)** It's a statement of a company's cash flows.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=65)** - [Interviewer] So, just a report of cash in, cash out?
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=67)** - [Expert] That's pretty much it.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=68)** - So, the three primary financial statements are the balance sheet, the income statement, and the statement of cash flows.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/what-are-the-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=74)** - Perfect.
>

#### The balance sheet
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - The balance sheet is a listing of a company's assets, its resources, its valuable things.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=5)** Its cash, its land, its inventory, the things that it holds to sale.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=10)** Those are its assets.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=11)** And the other part of the balance sheet is the listing of where the company got the money to buy those assets, the liabilities and the equities.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=18)** The balance sheet embodies The Accounting Equation, one of the greatest inventions of the human mind, invented in Italy over 500 years ago.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=26)** A listing of the assets, which is easy, anybody can list assets.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=30)** But the insight is to then also list where we get the money to buy those assets, the liabilities and the equities.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=35)** That's the balance sheet.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=37)** Now, assets.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=38)** They're valuable resources.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=40)** Cash, for example.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=41)** If you look at the balance sheet of Apple, you see that Apple has lots of cash for some very interesting reasons that I'd love to talk about at some length, but maybe some other time, we'll meet offline.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=51)** Accounts Receivable, money that is owed by other people to a company.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=56)** That's an asset.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=57)** Land, buildings, equipment, all of these are resources that a company uses in accomplishing its objectives.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=63)** Those are the assets.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=65)** Liabilities are obligations to repay money, or to provide a service in the future.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=70)** So Walmart for example, where does Walmart get most of its inventory, the things that Walmart has on its shelves to sell to you and me?
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=78)** Suppliers finance it.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=79)** Suppliers say, "You can pay us later."
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=81)** We call those Accounts Payable.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=83)** The second source of financing to buy assets is Owner's Equity, money provided to the company by the owners.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=89)** And owners can do this in two general ways.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=91)** One is that the owners can take money out of their personal savings and put it in the company, they've been working for years, saving a thousand dollars here, a thousand dollars there, now they put it in the company.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=101)** We call that Paid-In Capital.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=103)** That's one way that owners invest in their company.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=106)** A second way that owners invest in a company is by keeping profits of the company in the business, we call this Retained Earnings.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=113)** The profits of a business belong to the owners.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=116)** The owners can take those profits out and use them to buy groceries, or to buy a boat, or whatever else they want to do.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=121)** Or the owners can say, "Let's put those profits back in the business."
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=124)** We call that Retained Earnings.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=126)** Paid-In Capital and Retained Earnings are the amount of money that are provided to the company by the owners, to then buy assets.
>

>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=297)** Walmart is almost twice as large as Google in terms of assets.
>

>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=305)** How can it be that Walmart is such a bigger company than Google, even though the shareholders of both companies have put in about the same amount of money?
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=313)** Also, I want you to look at Citibank.

>

>

>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=322)** And yet the investment by the investors, the owners of Citibank, is not that large.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=327)** Where does Citibank get all the money to buy its assets?
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=332)** Well, maybe you didn't know this, from you and from me.
>
> **[5:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=335)** The depositors at Citibank, the people who deposit their money in Citibank are the primary providers of money to Citibank.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=342)** They owe use money.
>
> **[5:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=343)** We are liabilities as far as Citibank is concerned.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=346)** That's how banks are so large.
>
> **[5:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=348)** Small owner investment, but large amounts of assets.
>
> **[5:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=352)** So, we've got these six balance sheets for real companies.
>
> **[5:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=356)** And in each case, assets equal liabilities plus equity.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=359)** If you've got assets, you had to get the money somewhere to buy those assets.
>
> **[6:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=362)** And that's true for Citibank, for Walmart, for Apple, or for that corner drugstore.
>
> **[6:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=367)** You've got assets, you got to get the money to buy those assets from somewhere.
>
> **[6:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=370)** And those relationships, which assets, in what mix, and where did we get the money to buy those assets?
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=376)** Those tell very important things about a business, its strengths, its weaknesses, and its risks.
>
> **[6:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=382)** We're going to use the balance sheet in financial ratio analysis.
>
> **[6:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-balance-sheet-2?u=76281980&t=385)** The balance sheet, the mother of all financial statements.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** let (6), this, (2), finally, (1), case, (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1), we call this (1)
> **Analogies:** for example (2)
> **CLI Commands:** make (1)

#### The income statement
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - The second primary financial statement is the income statement.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=3)** Revenues minus expenses equals net income.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=7)** We use the terms revenues and expenses all the time, so let's make sure we know what these words mean.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=12)** In an accounting context revenue means the amount of assets generated in doing business.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=17)** And different companies generate assets in different ways.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=21)** Walmart for example generates assets by putting things on shelves that you and I buy, Walmart's inventory.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=27)** We pay Walmart for those things.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=28)** That's how Walmart creates assets.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=31)** Microsoft creates assets by creating software and hardware that you and I then buy.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=36)** And we pay Microsoft for those things.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=38)** Disney has consumer products.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=40)** They have cruises, they theme parks.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=43)** We pay to use those things, or to buy those products, and that's how Disney generates assets.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=49)** Revenue is the amount of assets generated in doing business.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=53)** Hopefully the assets generated are less than the assets consumed.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=57)** Expenses are the amount of assets consumed in doing business.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=61)** For example Microsoft consumes assets by paying programmers, by paying for equipment.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=65)** Walmart consumes assets by buying the inventory that sells to you and me, and paying rent, by seeing its buildings to depreciate, by paying its employees.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=74)** McDonald's consumes resources by buying food, buying paper, by renting facilities.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=79)** In each case, the revenues hopefully are more than the expenses that are consumed in generating business.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=87)** All of the this is put together in the income statement.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=89)** Net income, revenues minus expenses equal net income.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=93)** Net income is a very sophisticated economic measure.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=96)** It's the net amount of assets generated by a business through its business operations.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=101)** This is the income statement.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=103)** Let's look at some income statement examples for some companies of which you've heard.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=108)** Apple, and Google, and Microsoft, and Facebook, and Alibaba, and Walmart.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=116)** All of these companies have income statements that they release to the public on a regular basis.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=122)** Now take a look at these.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=123)** First of all, again, you see a difference in scale.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=125)** And take a look at those Facebook numbers.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=127)** They're so small compared to many of the others, but we talk about Facebook so much.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=133)** This illustrates an important point.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=134)** The financial statements are only one measure of a company's performance.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=138)** A very important measure, but only one measure.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=140)** Why do we talk about Facebook so often?
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=142)** Because Facebook, it's operations now are only a small fraction of what we think they're going to be in the future.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=148)** Facebook is expected to grow substantially in the future, so we talk about them a lot.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=152)** Alibaba is the largest e-commerce business in China.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=156)** And even though its numbers now are small, because it's the preeminent e-commerce business in China, it's expected to grow exponentially in the future.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=164)** So their income statement now is small, but we talk about them a lot.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=167)** Now look at those relationships.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=168)** Look at Google, and Microsoft, and Walmart.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=172)** Their incomes are about the same, within a few billion dollars of one another.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=176)** And yet, look at how large Walmart's sales are.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=179)** Why does Walmart have to sell so much to generate the same income as Google and Microsoft generate with much smaller sales?
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=187)** Well, that's the kind of thing we need to learn through doing financial ratio analysis.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=192)** To do our ratio analysis, let's use the income statement for a hypothetical company, Uncertain Company.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=198)** Sales, that's their revenues, minus their expenses, cost of goods sold, wage expense, research and development expense, and advertising expense leaving net income of $700.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=208)** We're going to use this income statement for Uncertain Company to understand is this company earning lots of money, or a little money?
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=214)** And if it's not very much, why not?
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=216)** Which expenses are causing problems?
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-income-statement-2?u=76281980&t=218)** The income statement, the second of the primary financial statements.

#### The statement of cash flows
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - Third primary financial statement is the statement of cash flows.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=4)** Conceptually, a statement of cash flows is quite simple.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=7)** Cash in, cash out.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=9)** The insight of accountants is to separate those cash flows into three categories.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=13)** Operating activities, investing activities, and financing activities.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=17)** Those three categories of cash flows are what are reported in the statement of cash flows.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=23)** Operating activities are what companies do every single day.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=26)** Collect cash from customers, pay cash to buy inventory, pay cash to employees, pay cash for rent, for advertising, for research and development.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=36)** All those things are operating activities.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=38)** Think of operating activities as the things that a business does every single day.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=42)** And hopefully a company would generate cash from its operating activities.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=46)** You would hope that a business would be collecting more cash than it's spending on a daily basis.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=51)** The second category in the statement of cash flows is investing activities.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=55)** This investing means investing in the productive capacity of the business.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=60)** Buying machines, buying land, buying buildings.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=64)** Those are investing activities.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=66)** In contrast to operating activities, which happen every single day, investing activities happen occasionally.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=72)** You don't buy land and buildings every single day.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=74)** You do that on occasion.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=76)** Operating activities, things that a business does every day.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=79)** Investing activities, investing in the productive capacity of business, happens occasionally.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=84)** The third category in the statement of cash flows is financing activities, and this is exactly what it sounds like.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=91)** Financing, borrowing money, repaying those loans, getting cash from investors, paying dividends to investors, getting the capital or financing to buy the assets that a business needs.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=103)** A way to think of the statement of cash flows is, financing activities, I'm getting the financing, the capital, to buy the assets, the investing activities, to then conduct the operations, the operating activities.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=113)** These are the things that a business does.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=115)** The statement of cash flows is built around operating, investing, and financing activities.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=122)** Let's look at examples of the statement of cash flows for six companies about which you may have heard.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=127)** Coca-Cola, ExxonMobil, Gazprom, which is the largest natural gas producer in the world, based in Russia, Facebook, Tesla, a maker of electric cars, and Walmart.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=139)** First thing I want you to look at is look at the statement of cash flows for ExxonMobil and for Gazprom.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=144)** Particularly look at their investing activities.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=147)** Billions upon billions of dollars of investing activities, investing in the productive capacity of these businesses.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=153)** These businesses need large machines and buildings and equipment and lots of land, and you see that reflected in the investing cash outflows of Gazprom and ExxonMobil.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=164)** These are often called capital expenditures.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=168)** Now I want you to look at the statement of cash flows for Coca-Cola and Walmart.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=172)** We call these cash cows.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=175)** The reason we call them cash cows is their operations generate more than enough cash to pay for all their investing activities, with cash left over.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=183)** They're generating cash.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=185)** Wouldn't you like to be a personal cash cow, where your daily cash flows were enough to pay for all your cars and houses and land and everything else you needed to buy in cash?
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=196)** That's Coca-Cola, that's Walmart.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=199)** Finally, look at the statement of cash flows for Tesla.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=202)** Tesla's a startup company, it's still growing.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=204)** And yes, its operations generate just enough to cash to pay for its investing activities, but still it's growing, it's investing, and therefore it is needing constant cash inflows from the providers of capital, from banks and from investors.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=218)** So you see large cash inflows from financing activities for Tesla.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=223)** This is characteristic of a startup company.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=226)** Now, I have some bad news about the statement of cash flows.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=229)** You're going to have to say goodbye to the statement of cash flows at this point, because most financial ratio analysis is done without cash flow ratios.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=238)** The reason for this is that the cash flow statement is so new.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=240)** It's less than 30 years old.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=242)** In contrast, the balance sheet and income statement are over 500 years old.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=246)** So the standard financial statement and ratio analysis formulas don't really include financial ratios related to cash flow.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=255)** Don't blame me, don't blame my brother.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=257)** The cash flow statement is just too new.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=260)** The balance sheet, the income statement, the statement of cash flows.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=263)** Those are the three primary financial statements.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-statement-of-cash-flows-2?u=76281980&t=266)** In our ratio analysis we'll focus on the first two, the balance sheet and the income statement.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** new. (2), let (1), finally, (1)
> **Speakers:** - third (1)


### 3. The DuPont Framework

> [↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### The DuPont company: creating accounting history
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=0)** - Kay, have you ever heard of the DuPont company?
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=3)** - Of course I have.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=4)** - Can you name some of their famous products?
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=6)** - Yes, I can.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=7)** Some of the well-known products invented in DuPont's laboratories include nylon, which was accidentally discovered when DuPont's chemists were seeing how far they could stretch polyester fibers, Teflon and SilverStone, which are non-stick finishes, Kevlar, which is used in bulletproof vests, and Lyrca, which is a spandex fiber.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=25)** - Okay, try this one, what was DuPont's first product?
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=29)** - Well, the original Monsieur DuPont came to United States from France and established a gunpowder factory near Wilmington, Delaware.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=37)** - All right, you seem to have some knowledge of the DuPont company, so tell us, why is DuPont famous in the field of financial ratio analysis?
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=47)** - Over 100 years ago, an accountant at DuPont, F. Donaldson Brown, created a way for a company to compare operating performance in various different divisions.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=56)** - So why was this such a big deal?
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=58)** - Well, DuPont was a vertically integrated company, and management often had to compare really different projects.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=63)** For example, they would have to decide whether to spend money to improve their manufacturing processes to lower cost, or to use that same money to streamline their purchasing process, so they could hold less inventory.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=75)** - So, how does this F. Donaldson Brown come into this?
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=79)** - Mr. Brown created a financial ratio analysis framework that combined measures of profitability and efficiency into one overall measure of performance.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=89)** - So what's this framework called?
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=91)** - The DuPont framework.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/the-dupont-company-creating-accounting-history?u=76281980&t=92)** - Well, let's learn about it.

#### DuPont framework
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - Okay, as we saw, Uncertain had a return on equity of 9.3%.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=5)** Not good.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=7)** Benchmark had a return on equity of 20.3%.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=10)** Very good.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=11)** Now, anybody can see that Benchmark is higher than Uncertain when it comes to return on equity.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=17)** Turns out, we can now be either a problem pointer or a problem solver.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=22)** Anybody can see that Uncertain has a problem.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=25)** What we want to know now is why do they have a problem, and that brings us, in all its glory, to the DuPont framework.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=34)** Now, the DuPont framework has these three components: profitability, efficiency, and leverage.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=40)** When it comes to leverage, that's an indication of how much money have we borrowed to purchase assets, and why do we purchase assets?
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=46)** We purchase assets in hopes of generating sales.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=50)** The leverage measure tells us how many assets we've been able to acquire with the equity that's been put in the company.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=57)** It gives us a measure of how much we've borrowed to buy assets, and why do we buy assets?
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=61)** To generate sales.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=62)** That's what the efficiency ratio is measuring.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=65)** We buy assets to generate sales.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=67)** The more sales we can generate per dollar of assets, the better.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=72)** And why do we want sales?
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=74)** That leads us to our profitability measure.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=76)** The more sales we have, the higher our income is going to be.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=79)** So first of all, we borrow money to buy assets.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=83)** We buy assets to generate sales.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=86)** We generate sales to generate net income.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=89)** Our return on equity measure tells us how much income did we generate given a fixed amount of stockholders' equity that's been invested by the owners in the firm.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=99)** Now, with that framework, let's take a look at Uncertain versus Benchmark, and use the DuPont framework to identify not only how Uncertain has done but why have they performed, particularly relative to Benchmark.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=115)** So we can see the two companies return on equity and DuPont framework ratios here.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=121)** Uncertain with 9.3%, Benchmark with 20.3%.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=125)** And the first thing we noticed was that leverage wasn't an issue.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=129)** Leverage was the same for both companies, so in explaining the difference in return on equity between Uncertain and Benchmark, it can't be attributed to leverage.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=137)** So then we looked at efficiency, and it turns out we found out that Uncertain generates $1.38 in sales for each dollar's worth of assets it has compared to Benchmark which generates $1.70 in sales for every dollar's worth of assets that they have.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=154)** Benchmark is much more efficient at generating sales with its assets than is Uncertain.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=160)** Then we looked at profitability.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=162)** When it came to profitability, Uncertain was generating $3.5 in profit for every hundred dollars in sales compared to Benchmark which was generating $6.2 in profit for every hundred dollars' worth of sales.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=175)** So why was Benchmark's return on equity so much higher than Uncertain's?
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=182)** Profitability and efficiency.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=185)** Benchmark is much better at generating sales with its assets and generating earnings with the sales that it has.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=192)** So now, do we have any other questions?

>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=202)** Which expenses are too high which would account for their lower profitability?
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/running-a-profitable-business-understanding-financial-ratios/dupont-framework-2?u=76281980&t=206)** We want to know the answer to those questions and we will do further analysis to get there.
